<div id="review_2020553624" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2020553624" />
    <a title="edge of bubble" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/55519430-edge-of-bubble"><img alt="edge of bubble" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1496688756p2/55519430.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2020553624?book_show_action=true">Jun 06, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="edge of bubble" class="user" itemprop="url" name="edge of bubble" href="/user/show/55519430-edge-of-bubble">edge of bubble</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/55519430-edge-of-bubble?shelf=funny">funny</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/55519430-edge-of-bubble?shelf=buddy-read">buddy-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/55519430-edge-of-bubble?shelf=lovely-covers">lovely-covers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/55519430-edge-of-bubble?shelf=2017">2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/55519430-edge-of-bubble?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/55519430-edge-of-bubble?shelf=disappointment">disappointment</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2020553624" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17770598531373859115">massive buddy-read with <s>cheaters who started the book early</s> amazing people.<br/><br/><br/><b>
  <i>The cake is a lie.</i>
</b><br/><br/><br/>Looking at the reviews, I could find just one review under 4 stars rating and I know only <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1927755889?book_show_action=false&from_review_page=1' rel='nofollow noopener'>one person</a> who didn't fall head over heels in love with this book. So welcome to my verra <s>bitchy</s> lonely <i>I liked this book, but over all, it was a disappointing experience</i> review.<br/><br/>I adored KoW for the first 100 pages or so. The feelies every word evoked, the adorable humour, the interesting setting and most of all</span>
  <span id="freeText17770598531373859115" style="display:none">massive buddy-read with <s>cheaters who started the book early</s> amazing people.<br><br><br><b>
  <i>The cake is a lie.</i>
</b><br><br><br>Looking at the reviews, I could find just one review under 4 stars rating and I know only <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1927755889?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">one person</a> who didn't fall head over heels in love with this book. So welcome to my verra <s>bitchy</s> lonely <i>I liked this book, but over all, it was a disappointing experience</i> review.<br><br>I adored KoW for the first 100 pages or so. The feelies every word evoked, the adorable humour, the interesting setting and most of all, the amazing writing... Almost everyone in the buddy-read was having a great time with a lot of laughs, but I think my emotion patches were malfunctioning, since it was mostly sadness with a chuckle here and there for me. Still, it was a great read, in a different way.<br><br>But The Cuckold King aka Matty broke the spell. I disliked him and seeing the shallowness of his character caused me to look at the others with my <i>bitchy-coloured glasses</i> too.<br><br>Basically, the whole plot felt like a recyled monster fight, fought by unkillable bots in a game choke full of every fantasy creature the author could think of. There is even a chapter named "Sheer Dumb Luck" that summarises what's going on, quite well.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1497488010ra/23028241.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>our heroes *on the left* vs anyone and everyone *on the right*</i><br><br>If, this book wasn't the most hyped book I've seen in GR to date, with splendid reviews that kept raising the expectations for me, I might have enjoyed it more. But phrases like "<i>a mixture of Joe Abercrombie and Scott Lynch and Patrick Rothfuss</i>" in almost every review, set the bar very high, took this book out of the "parody" box to a more serious line. And led me to believe that I was about to read a book which tackled serious concepts in a non serious way, that there would be a hidden depth to the story. Something would come out of the pages and slap me with a <b>WOW</b> so hard, I'd drown in my amazement. But what I got was the same rthym;<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1497488010ra/23028241.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1497488010ra/23028242.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And then;<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1497488010ra/23028243.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I absolutely hate it when heroes/heroines die in a book, after all the emotions I invest in them, it affects me bad. Usually, I get sad about even side characters' death. But here, I wish all of them had died. And somehow, their deaths was the thing that set the epic ending to motion. I would be mad, call the author some unsavory names, but also call this book a masterpiece of debut novels. Because there's great imagination and writing here!<br><br>Another thing that went over my head was the references to songs, games etc. I only caught one or two, and of course "<b>
  <i>the cake is a lie</i>
</b>" line. And that's ironic, in a way. Would I be amazed with this book, and overlook the lack of depth in the story, if I was able to discern those secret messages / be a fan of those games? I don't know. But <a href="https://nicholaseames.com/soundtrack/" rel="nofollow noopener">the tasteful soundtrack list author has posted in his website</a>, definetely upped my enjoyement.<br><br>I loved buddy reading with everyone, but this experience made me realise, that I am a shitty buddy reader and others' reactions sometimes changes my expectations and make me doubt my own reactions. So I will go back to lurking in group read threads for the books I'm enjoying but will not join another one, unless it is just one or two people.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17770598531373859115" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer7130313384406157590"><b>Bloody fantastic!!! All the stars!</b><br/><br/>I’m going to tell you all a big secret of mine. You ready?<br/>I’m great at reading epic fantasty books but I’m <b>down right terrible at reviewing them!</b><br/>The secret is out! ¯\_(ツ)_/¯<br/><br/>So here goes!<br/><br/><b>Kings of the Wyld</b> was one of the best fantasy books that I’ve read in years. From all the great characte</span>
  <span id="freeText7130313384406157590" style="display:none"><b>Bloody fantastic!!! All the stars!</b><br><br>I’m going to tell you all a big secret of mine. You ready?<br>I’m great at reading epic fantasty books but I’m <b>down right terrible at reviewing them!</b><br>The secret is out! ¯\_(ツ)_/¯<br><br>So here goes!<br><br><b>Kings of the Wyld</b> was one of the best fantasy books that I’ve read in years. It had the perfect balance of humor, camaraderie and action all in one fantastic book!<br>Honestly, I wish I could give this more then <b>5 stars</b> because I loved everything about it! From all the great characters in the band, the monsters, the journey through Heartwyld, to the ending.<br><br>I’m actually not sure which character was my favorite from Clay Cooper who’s the reliable and cautious member of the group Saga, or the funny and brilliant Moog who’s the magician of the band.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1564678071i/27924526._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Saga was the name of the band that Clay Cooper, Moog, Gabriel, Matrick and Ganelon were apart of when they were younger, tougher and crazier.<br>They would go into the Heartwyld, which is a huge forest with every type of scary and crazy monster hiding in it. They would forge together as a team, capture the beast and rid the surrounding area of whatever was killing people. It could be a dragon, a horde of centaurs, a chimera, to a crazy cyclops. This book had every cool and great monster/beast in it!<br><br>Now Saga has been disbanded. The members are all older, fatter, drunk or just don’t have the heart to battle anything these days.<br><br><b>Kings of the Wyld</b> starts off with Gabriel showing up on Clay’s door asking for help in rescuing his daughter from a horde of monsters that has surrounded the city of Castia.<br>The castle and city are in ruins and people are dying everyday from the monsters and beasts.<br><br>Gabriel finds a way to talk Clay into making one last stand and journey through the wilds of the Heartwyld again. But first, in order to do this impossible task, they’ve got to get the band back together!<br><br><b>Kings of the Wyld</b> had a great rock and roll vibe to this book along with excellent dialogue and well thought out world building.<br><br>Would I recommend this book? Your fucking sweet ass I would!! I can’t wait to read the next book in the series, <b>Bloody Rose</b>!<br><br>Seriously, kudos <i>Nicholas Eames</i> on writing one of the best well rounded, funny, and action packed books with tons of heart! I would laugh so hard my sides would hurt and then next, I would be sad and crushed by some of the dialogue between the band members.<br>It's just great writing and characterization.<br><br><b>And yeah Moog, I want an owlbear now too.</b> hahaha!<br><b>It can’t get much better in the fantasy genre then this!</b></span>

<div id="review_1961670449" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1961670449" />
    <a title="TS Chan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30279227-ts-chan"><img alt="TS Chan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1543800303p2/30279227.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1961670449?book_show_action=true">Sep 03, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="TS Chan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="TS Chan" href="/user/show/30279227-ts-chan">TS Chan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/31698361-kings-of-the-wyld">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to TS by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/59458347-petrik">Petrik</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30279227-ts-chan?shelf=physical-owned">physical-owned</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1961670449" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16424439322246567692">In a year full of impressive fantasy debuts, Kings of The Wyld earned itself a top spot among the greats.<br/><br/>As I have not been gaming for almost two decades now, a lot of the RPG and Final Fantasy references did not click with me. Regardless, I still had an awesome time reading this book. Unlike Ready Player One which I found to be enjoyable mainly because of the 80s pop culture references, Kings of the Wyld resonated with me because of its characters and story.<br/> <br/>I did get the homage to the music ba</span>
  <span id="freeText16424439322246567692" style="display:none">In a year full of impressive fantasy debuts, Kings of The Wyld earned itself a top spot among the greats.<br><br>As I have not been gaming for almost two decades now, a lot of the RPG and Final Fantasy references did not click with me. Regardless, I still had an awesome time reading this book. Unlike Ready Player One which I found to be enjoyable mainly because of the 80s pop culture references, Kings of the Wyld resonated with me because of its characters and story.<br> <br>I did get the homage to the music bands of old vs the recent ones (it's been over 30 years since I've fallen in love with Duran Duran and am proud to see them still going strong). And being in that demographic group, I can't help but agree that the overall quality of the bands back in the day was much better. While I am not saying that there are no standouts in the modern era, they are but far and few in between. Ok, I am digressing. <br><br>The characters are the highlight of this novel. I pretty much loved every band member of Saga. Even though the story was told solely from the third person perspective of Clay Cooper, I was still able to know the other band members well enough to appreciate their characterisation. Just when I thought that I found my favourite character, one or another will do or say something that makes me love him just as much. Gabriel, Moog, Matrick and Ganelon are all awesome in their own unique way and that solid bond of friendship between these guys is truly touching. Even the supporting characters, notably a revenant and a two-headed monster, were highly likeable. Eames also gave us a villain which I can completely empathise with. <br><br><i>
  <b>
    <blockquote>As individuals they were each of them fallible, discordant as notes without harmony. But as a band they were something more, something perfect in its own intangible way.</blockquote>
  </b>
</i><br>Of course, great characters alone do not make a good tale. What was most compelling to me was the beautiful simplicity of the story. It was a story of a father's love for his daughter. And behind that, a friend's love, compassion and empathy. Eames then took that simple story that was full of heart and made it utterly entertaining with two killer ingredients; humour and mythological monsters. <br><br>With a blend of sarcastic and ironic humour, sometimes crude or laced with innuendos, and occasionally slapstick even, the narrative never ventured too far into grimness before it drew me back with laughter. <br><br>While a lot of the gaming references flew over my head, I did appreciate and enjoy how the world was built upon almost every mythological monster in the fantasy genre - be it in books or games. Some which I'd come across back during my teenage years when I used to immerse myself in Fighting Fantasy books by Steve Jackson and Ian Livingstone. <br><br>Remember these?<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1504950331i/23849127._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Eames has a prose and writing style that engages the reader without too much flourish that can distract from an immersive experience. With good pacing and well-written action scenes, the pages just flew by whenever I pick up the book. While this is the first book in a series, it can be read on its own as its ending wrapped up the story satisfactorily. <br><br>All in all, a fantastic read that is full of heart and loads of rollicking fun.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16424439322246567692" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Hamad" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/54464244-hamad"><img alt="Hamad" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577880699p2/54464244.jpg" /></a>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2761616535" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer318504695173134951">This review and other non-spoilery reviews can be found <a href='https://thebookprescription.wordpress.com/2019/07/08/kings-of-the-wyld-review/' rel='nofollow noopener'>@The Book Prescription</a><br/><br/><b>Actual Rating: 4.25-4.5 stars</b><br/><br/> <b>
  <i>“WHEN WE SEEK TO RULE ONLY OURSELVES, WE ARE EACH OF US KINGS.” </i>
</b><br/><br/>🌟 If you have been following my latest posts, and specifically my book discussions. I talked about my YA crisis in the latest one and how books are all becoming the same to me. I have been reading more adult books and Kings of the Wyld have been on my radar for a while. It has been getting mostly good reviews and I think i</span>
  <span id="freeText318504695173134951" style="display:none">This review and other non-spoilery reviews can be found <a href="https://thebookprescription.wordpress.com/2019/07/08/kings-of-the-wyld-review/" rel="nofollow noopener">@The Book Prescription</a><br /><br /><b>Actual Rating: 4.25-4.5 stars</b><br /><br /> <b>
  <i>“WHEN WE SEEK TO RULE ONLY OURSELVES, WE ARE EACH OF US KINGS.” </i>
</b><br /><br />🌟 If you have been following my latest posts, and specifically my book discussions. I talked about my YA crisis in the latest one and how books are all becoming the same to me. I have been reading more adult books and Kings of the Wyld have been on my radar for a while. It has been getting mostly good reviews and I think it deserves the hype.<br /><br />🌟 What is this book about? I feel I can’t pass the opportunity to explain this because this is very unusual and very new. Contrary to the common sterotypical main characters in literature, the characters here were famous back in the day. They were one of the most famous mercenary groups called Saga, the group basically disassembled and now they are getting back together for one more adventure!<br /><br />🌟 The writing is unique and I am not sure if it can be called satire as I have never read that but it certainly was hilarious. To mix fantasy with humor is quite a daunting task because they are 2 polar opposites and the author did a great job in getting a good balance. It kind of had the Funny but serious Marvel movies vibes to it. Sometimes I would have preferred if the author took a more serious tone because it would have worked a little bit better than humor. However, for most of the book, I did enjoy it and did not mind it. However, I think readers should go into it expecting this.<br /><br /> <b>
  <i> “You should write a book,” Matrick suggested.<br /><br /> Kit snorted. “Who wants to read the self-pitying lamentations of an old revenant?”<br /><br /> “There’s your title right there,” said Ganelon.” </i>
</b><br /><br />🌟 The characters were my favorite part of the story, we have old, fat, drunk, loud, obnoxious and silly old men who were glorious back in the day. Clay is the nice one, Gabe is a leader, Moog is my favorite and is like the comic relief in the group, Ganelon is the powerful one and Matrick is a drunk cuckold king. Talk about creativity!!<br /><br /> <b>
  <i> “As individuals they were each of them fallible, discordant as notes without harmony. But as a band they were something more, something perfect in its own intangible way” </i>
</b><br /><br />🌟 The pacing is good, It was not fast but it did not stretch out either. The endings of each chapter left me wanting more and more and so it was easier to go through than expected. I need to mention that chapter 49 was AMAZING!!! And the last chapters after that were all great.<br /><br />🌟 Summary: Kings of the Wyld was an unusual read in a very good way. I like the writing, the characters and the whole idea of this book is just creative. I also liked the closure of the story and it left me completely satisfied. I will be getting Bloody Rose and reading it soon! </span>
  <a data-text-id="318504695173134951" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1947160208" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1947160208" />
    <a title="Celeste" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7317186-celeste"><img alt="Celeste" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1481055226p2/7317186.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1947160208?book_show_action=true">Dec 07, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Celeste" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Celeste" href="/user/show/7317186-celeste">Celeste</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7317186-celeste?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7317186-celeste?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7317186-celeste?shelf=funny">funny</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1947160208" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4356400777607315374"><i>You can find <a href='https://wp.me/pa0WBY-ni' rel='nofollow noopener'>this</a> review and more at <a href='http://novelnotions.net' rel='nofollow noopener'>Novel Notions</a>. </i><br/><br/><strong>Man, <em>this was so much fun</em>!!</strong><br/><br/>First of all, <u>I <em>love</em> classic rock</u>. Like, a lot. Seriously, the soundtrack of my childhood consisted largely of Queen, Journey, Styx, Foreigner, and other bands of their ilk. Saturday mornings are still meant for “Your Love” by The Outfield and “Jessie’s Girl” by Rick Springfield.<br/><br/>So, when my friends started gushing about a fantasy novel filled with musical references from one of my favorite eras, and promising that it </span>
  <span id="freeText4356400777607315374" style="display:none"><i>You can find <a href="https://wp.me/pa0WBY-ni" rel="nofollow noopener">this</a> review and more at <a href="http://novelnotions.net" rel="nofollow noopener">Novel Notions</a>. </i><br /><br /><strong>Man, <em>this was so much fun</em>!!</strong><br /><br />First of all, <u>I <em>love</em> classic rock</u>. Like, a lot. Seriously, the soundtrack of my childhood consisted largely of Queen, Journey, Styx, Foreigner, and other bands of their ilk. Saturday mornings are still meant for “Your Love” by The Outfield and “Jessie’s Girl” by Rick Springfield.<br /><br />So, when my friends started gushing about a fantasy novel filled with musical references from one of my favorite eras, and promising that it was funny to boot, I added it to my list. But something else always seemed to grab my attention, and it stayed unread on my list for months. That is, until my lovely friend <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/59458347-petrik" rel="nofollow noopener">Petrik</a> sent me a copy as a surprise early Christmas gift. With my very own copy in hand, I finally cracked KotW open. And I’m so glad that I did!<br /><br /><strong>I don’t know that I have ever described a book as “rollicking” but this one definitely was.</strong> "What if mercenaries were treated like the rock bands of the fantasy world?" is basically the best jumping off point for any book ever. The use of music industry terms, like headliner and touring and booker and frontman, were all really fun additions. I’m in a band, so seeing a band equivalent in a fantasy setting was exciting and incredibly entertaining for me. Also, I <em>loved</em> all of the band and song references. I know there’s no way I caught them all, but any time I did catch one I was messaging friends with cyber squeals of joy. I’ll refrain from giving any away, because the search for musical Easter eggs is half the fun!<br /><br />And the music references weren’t the only ones Eames included. Video games and and movies and classic fantasy novels were all referenced, as well. Here’s my favorite, a reference to The Hobbit:<br /><blockquote>“The place was a hovel, but not the cozy hovel of the sort inhabited by poets and scribes, crammed with bookshelves, candles, and antique curios. Nor was it the sparse kind of hovel, occupied by little more than a ragged blanket and a straw-stuffed mattress: It was a kubold’s hovel, and that meant shithole.”</blockquote><br /><u>I genuinely busted out laughing when I read that paragraph, and it makes me smile every time I remember it.</u> There are so many lines like that in this book. But <b>there was also depth here, lines that actually made me stop and think, which stood out all the more because of the predominant humor throughout the majority of the book.</b> For example:<br /><blockquote>“But what does a mirror know? What can it show us of ourselves? Oh, it might reveal a few scars, and perhaps a glimpse—there, in the eyes—of our true nature. The spirit beneath the skin. Yet the deepest scars are often hidden, and though a mirror might reveal our weakness, it reflects only a fraction of our strength.”</blockquote><br />See? That’s deep stuff, man. And that deep thought sprung right from the head of our main protagonist, “Slowhand” Clay Cooper. I enjoyed Clay so much. <strong>I loved all of the members of Saga, a classic band getting together for one last adventure and the central focus of the book. But Clay was definitely my favorite.</strong> If Saga is to be equated with an actual musical band, here are my thoughts on what instrument each member would play. Golden Gabe is the frontman, as we already know from the book itself, but the rest are all strictly my opinion. I believe that Ganelon is the lead guitarist, because lead guitarists of rock bands tend to be destructive and more than a little crazy and are often lady magnets, all of which apply. Moog plays the synthesizer, because he’s kooky and does his own thing but it somehow always works out with what the rest of the band is doing. Matty Skulldrummer would have to be the drummer for obvious reasons.<br /><br />That leaves Clay. I think Slowhand is an appropriate stage name for a bassist. A bassist tends to be the binding agent in a band, the person who quietly holds everything together and keeps the song moving in the right direction. <strong>The bass-line is the heartbeat of a song, and Clay Cooper is without a doubt the heartbeat of Saga. Also, I have a thing for bassists; my husband is a phenomenal one.</strong><br /><br />All of that randomness to say: <u>I <em>really</em> loved this book</u>. And honestly, I could go on about the employment of such a wide array of fantastical creatures and magical weapons and intriguing mythology, but I want to leave as much as possible unknown for others to discover for themselves. There were a couple of writing choices that I would have changed, like doing away with a few of the plethora of similes employed in the prose, but there was nothing that bothered me enough to keep me from giving the book five rocking stars. <strong>If you’re looking for something that mingles humor with heart, that will make you feel nostalgic and keep you entertained as you search for various pop culture references, I’ve found no other novel that can top this one.</strong></span>
  <a data-text-id="4356400777607315374" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer11742278177985393238">No spoilers as the book isn't out yet, but this is a terrific read for fantasy fans who enjoy a mix of old-school adventuring told in a modern voice and with a rock and roll flair. Nicholas Eames knows how to take the tropes of heroic fantasy and simultaneously revel in them while often turning them on their head. Lots of fun to be had here.</span>

<div id="review_2007697668" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2007697668" />
    <a title="Michael Britt" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/51188905-michael-britt"><img alt="Michael Britt" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1513347398p2/51188905.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2007697668?book_show_action=true">May 29, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michael Britt" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michael Britt" href="/user/show/51188905-michael-britt">Michael Britt</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Michael by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/59458347-petrik">Petrik</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/51188905-michael-britt?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2007697668" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3283338584605190013">This book. THIS FREAKING BOOK! Man, I'm blown away, yet again, by another book this year. It's been a pretty amazing year of books, and this one comes very close to topping that list. <br/><br/><b>"Hit it like you hate it."</b><br/><br/>I'm convinced that Canada births some of the most gifted Fantasy writers. You've got Steven Erikson, Sebastian de Castell and now, added to that list, is Nicholas Eames. This is, quite possibly, my favorite debut novel. Right behind Traitor's Blade by Sebastian de Castell and Theft of Swor</span>
  <span id="freeText3283338584605190013" style="display:none">This book. THIS FREAKING BOOK! Man, I'm blown away, yet again, by another book this year. It's been a pretty amazing year of books, and this one comes very close to topping that list. <br /><br /><b>"Hit it like you hate it."</b><br /><br />I'm convinced that Canada births some of the most gifted Fantasy writers. You've got Steven Erikson, Sebastian de Castell and now, added to that list, is Nicholas Eames. This is, quite possibly, my favorite debut novel. Right behind Traitor's Blade by Sebastian de Castell and Theft of Swords by Michael J Sullivan. After dabbling so much in multiple POV books I've grown to not like first-person POV's quite as much. Since the person we're getting the POV from tends to either be a Gary Stue/Mary Sue (I think that's the right terminology) or extremely annoying. Eames had done something quite remarkable here and given us Clay Cooper: a protagonist that is flawed enough to seem real, but awesome enough that I never got sick of his POV. <br /><br />Something that can make or break a book for me is, by far, the characters. I can deal with a crappy plot, as long as the characters are well written. This book excelled in both areas. But I like to keep my reviews spoiler free so I'll focus on the characters in this section. We get this band of mercs that are among the best bromances I've ever read. They're hilarious, bad ass savages. It would be folly for me to try and pick my favorite. They each being their own awesomeness to the table. Seriously. Usually there is at least one character that's too perfect or just annoying. He has managed, like he did with Clay, to create a whole band full of unique characters that being something to the table to help strengthen the group. <br /><br />I thought the classic rock references would eventually get old, but to my surprise and satisfaction, he did it perfectly. Some hidden so well that you might miss the majority of them. Also, the video game feel you get from it is subtle enough that it doesn't over power the story, but you'll pick up on it if you've played these games. D&amp;D seeming to be one of the biggest influences.<br /><br />Now, to touch briefly on the story. I'll keep this spoiler free, as well. Eames has managed to create a story with the most perfect mix of grim dark and humor. It doesn't feel like he set out with a goal to write a grimdark story and I loved that. It was just a byproduct of the world he created. His prose is among some of the best, as well. He's managed to write a story vivid enough to make you feel like you're there, but it's tight and fast-paced enough for you to not get bored. To me, that seems like a tough thing for authors to balance. And he's done it so well. There were so many laugh out loud moments that I thought I was going to get kicked out of the coffee shop. <br /><br />I don't think I could ever do this book justice with a review. If you're a fan of Fantasy and have a love for classic rock or video games, pick this up, immediately. If you're just a fan of well-written Fantasy, pick this up, immediately!</span>
  <a data-text-id="3283338584605190013" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1839102593" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1839102593" />
    <a title="Petros Triantafyllou" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/35342421-petros-triantafyllou"><img alt="Petros Triantafyllou" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1839102593?book_show_action=true">Mar 06, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Petros Triantafyllou" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Petros Triantafyllou" href="/user/show/35342421-petros-triantafyllou">Petros Triantafyllou</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1839102593" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6573057612809420871">I may be taking a risk here, what with being still on March and all that, but I'll declare Kings of the Wyld debut of the year. <br/><br/>Clay Cooper leads a peaceful and quiet life. He takes some shifts in the City Watch, he drinks a couple of beers in the King's Head, and spends some quality time with his wife and daughter. Or at least he used to. Because right now he's robbed, hungry, on the road, and trying to do the unthinkable; re-unite his old mercenary band called Saga, cross a forest full of ever</span>
  <span id="freeText6573057612809420871" style="display:none">I may be taking a risk here, what with being still on March and all that, but I'll declare Kings of the Wyld debut of the year. <br /><br />Clay Cooper leads a peaceful and quiet life. He takes some shifts in the City Watch, he drinks a couple of beers in the King's Head, and spends some quality time with his wife and daughter. Or at least he used to. Because right now he's robbed, hungry, on the road, and trying to do the unthinkable; re-unite his old mercenary band called Saga, cross a forest full of every possible monster you have ever imagined and then some, and face a horde of one hundred thousand strong. What could possibly go wrong?<br /><br /><i>“But what does a mirror know? What can it show us of ourselves? Oh, it might reveal a few scars, and perhaps a glimpse—there, in the eyes—of our true nature. The spirit beneath the skin. Yet the deepest scars are often hidden, and though a mirror might reveal our weakness, it reflects only a fraction of our strength.” </i><br /><br />I started this review by saying that I'm taking a risk, but the true risk here was taken by the author. Eames wrote a story of tragedy and darkness, but in an amusing, humoristic and light-hearted tone. To do so without turning the work into a parody, talent and experience are required. Eames has the first but not the second. And yet, he pulled it off, and more than successfully so. <br /><br />Eames is excellent with prose, in fact one of the best that I've recently reviewed. He uses an intense "thriller-like" method of pacing which he successfully mixes with the humorous tone he introduced with a specific character's appearance. While Eames tells a straightforward story, he also gets into some strong explorations of the characters' characters, pasts and motivations, things that help to carry the story. He is also great in the small reversals of scene, especially those concerning the characters. You may dislike, even hate some of them, and then love them or realize that you were unfair. <br /><br />All in all, Kings of the Wyld is a pleasant, poignant, well-told and engaging story, and Nicholas Eames is a talented author who's here to stay. <br /><br />You can find more of my reviews over at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://BookNest.eu/">http://BookNest.eu/</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="6573057612809420871" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2677621637" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2677621637" />
    <a title="Markus" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/26681101-markus"><img alt="Markus" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1421952301p2/26681101.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2677621637?book_show_action=true">Jan 17, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Markus" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Markus" href="/user/show/26681101-markus">Markus</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26681101-markus?shelf=dungeons-and-dragons">dungeons-and-dragons</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26681101-markus?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2677621637" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1370295213927136156"><b>
  <i>“This is not a choice between life and death, but life and immortality! Remain here and die in obscurity, or follow me now and live forever!”</i>
</b><br/><br/>There are two ways to read this book, from what I can tell. You can read it as a fantasy novel (what it indeed may have been written as), and expect a stunning well-crafted narrative of epic proportions equal to the giants of fantasy literature. And you’ll be horribly disappointed when you notice all the aspects in which it falls flat. There is simply t</span>
  <span id="freeText1370295213927136156" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>“This is not a choice between life and death, but life and immortality! Remain here and die in obscurity, or follow me now and live forever!”</i>
</b><br /><br />There are two ways to read this book, from what I can tell. You can read it as a fantasy novel (what it indeed may have been written as), and expect a stunning well-crafted narrative of epic proportions equal to the giants of fantasy literature. And you’ll be horribly disappointed when you notice all the aspects in which it falls flat. There is simply too much inconsistency, flagrant use of deus ex machina, overused sexual humour and a story that essentially stops being good three quarters of the way through as the author decided he needed to wrap up quickly. That’s the first way.<br /><br />Alternatively, you can read it like the novelisation of a Dungeons &amp; Dragons campaign. This reading justifies nearly all of the above, your expectations are significantly lowered, and you can simply enjoy the book for what it seems to be.<br /><br />The evidence for the second reading being the best one should be plentiful and convincing: the setting has generic lands and kingdoms that nobody cares about and do not matter to the story. The story is centred on groups of adventurers practically functioning as heroic rockstars, even going so far as to have band names. We follow them adventure, make camp, be ambushed, fight random arrow fodder creatures, and indeed both enter dungeons and fight dragons. There are poorly veiled references to classic D&amp;D creatures, the humour is juvenile, there is a lot of modern references being close to breaking the fourth wall (including fantasy viagra), and there are artifacts with ridiculously unrealistic and unexplained names. And the author states clearly that the world of the Forgotten Realms is one of his biggest inspirations. It shows.<br /><br />The heroes are, of course, your average D&amp;D group. You can almost see them being played by a group of adventure-addicted young men in a dim suburban basement surrounded by half-eaten boxes of delivered pizza. Their DM has even deigned to give them all iconic magic weapons with illustrious backstories. This means, naturally, that they are hardly the deepest. They are cardboard cutouts with little in the way of personality except nostalgic heroism. But, as with any D&amp;D campaign, the splendour lies in the NPCs. <br /><br /><i>"After what happened to my parents, and what I did to those children, what could I have become but a monster?"</i><br /><br />Larkspur is the best of the bunch, and it is a rarity to read about a character whose role is improved by being hit in the head. Others are almost equally intriguing: the murdering adulterous queen with the laughably unimaginative name, the druins, dark and mysterious remnants of a mythic past, Jain the thieving bandit with a heart of gold, and on and on. The group’s undead bard (what a wonderful idea) is another example:<br /><br /><i>“You should write a book,” Matrick suggested. Kit snorted. “Who wants to read the self-pitying lamentations of an old revenant?” “There's your title right there,” said Ganelon.</i><br /><br />From the unrealistic and unbelievable to the straight up trashy (in a fun way); from references to World of Warcraft and The Elder Scrolls to the most fan service-heavy segments of any fantasy, this is a all-encompassing nerdy pop culture phenomenon more than anything else.<br /><br />Overall, <i>Kings of the Wyld</i> is not an excellent book in any technical way. It is not among the greats of the fantasy genre and it is not a memorable piece of literature. It will not win any hard-hitting awards, nor does it deserve them, but nor does it need them. What it is, however, is perhaps the finest ever example of turning the classical Dungeons &amp; Dragons experience into a novel. Nearly every attempt at this turns out a disaster, but Nicholas Eames succeeds.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1370295213927136156" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

<div id="review_2005368396" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2005368396" />
    <a title="Niki Hawkes - The Obsessive Bookseller" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13396599-niki-hawkes---the-obsessive-bookseller"><img alt="Niki Hawkes - The Obsessive Bookseller" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1517553177p2/13396599.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2005368396?book_show_action=true">May 20, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Niki Hawkes - The Obsessive Bookseller" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Niki Hawkes - The Obsessive Bookseller" href="/user/show/13396599-niki-hawkes---the-obsessive-bookseller">Niki Hawkes - The Obsessive Bookseller</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2005368396" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12315067345359291217">I read Kings of the Wyld as part of a Buddy Read with my favorite Goodreads group, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/topic/show/18617810-kings-of-the-wyld-june-august-2017' rel='nofollow noopener'>Fantasy Buddy Reads</a> (where the author even showed up to say a few gracious words – how cool is that?!). This is one of those unique books that got devoured as soon as it came across my radar. If you have any knowledge of my colossal TBR pile, you know that most things that land on it sit there for 5+ sometimes even 10+ years before it gets read. The premise for Kings of the Wyld sounded so interesting, I couldn’t </span>
  <span id="freeText12315067345359291217" style="display:none">I read Kings of the Wyld as part of a Buddy Read with my favorite Goodreads group, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/topic/show/18617810-kings-of-the-wyld-june-august-2017" rel="nofollow noopener">Fantasy Buddy Reads</a> (where the author even showed up to say a few gracious words – how cool is that?!). This is one of those unique books that got devoured as soon as it came across my radar. If you have any knowledge of my colossal TBR pile, you know that most things that land on it sit there for 5+ sometimes even 10+ years before it gets read. The premise for Kings of the Wyld sounded so interesting, I couldn’t pass up the opportunity to read it asap.<br><br>The book was <i>hysterical</i>.<br><br>And not just mildly amusing, but the kind of funny that still has me laughing at some of the moments several months later. To set the stage, a retired band of mercenaries (who have become old, fat, and in some cases drunk) pull themselves back together to go on a quest. The main character goes reluctantly, and his sardonic attitude towards <i>everything</i> is what gives this book such a strong voice. All of the characters were individualized and funny in their own way (my favorite of which being Arcandius Moog – the gay wizard who’s quite comfortable questing in a onesie, thank you very much), but they all had to put their differences and arguments aside to accomplish their goal. Add to that a ton of nerdy references, and you have one hella fun book!<br><br>What surprised me the most was not just the funny stuff, but how equal of an impact the more serious, deeper moments had on the story. They may have been far between, but the emotional investment I felt was just as strong as for a fantasy without all of the humor. It meant to me that Nicholas Eames was in it to write more than just a fun book – he also succeeded in producing one with substance. <br><br>I’ve discovered throughout the years that I am a somewhat inpatient reader. There are so many books on my TBR that it becomes increasingly difficult to stop everything and just enjoy each book for the journey it offers. Kings of the Wyld was mostly about the journey – the pacing focused more on character-building and humor than it did the destination (that is, until things got rolling near the end, then it didn’t let up). What I’m trying to say is, Kings of the Wyld reinvigorated my passion for discovering new authors, took me out of my carefully laid reading plans, and made me appreciate the journey for the first time in a long while.<br><br>Overall, this is going to be a very easy book for me to recommend. I can’t tell you how many times I’ve had customers ask me for a funny fantasy book and all I could do was point out two popular authors whose humor didn’t quite work for me (Piers Anthony and Terry Pratchett… masters of their genre, but not works that I could personally stand behind based on my own experience… don’t be mad at me.) Finally, I have the start to a killer fantasy with tons of humor and substance – one that I can recommend with confidence. If you’re sick of the same old stuff, or are in the mood for a good laugh – Kings of the Wyld is my pick for you!<br><br>Via The Obsessive Bookseller at <a href="http://www.nikihawkes.com" rel="nofollow noopener">www.NikiHawkes.com</a> <br><br>Other books you might like:<br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18947303.Traitor_s_Blade__Greatcoats___1_" title="Traitor's Blade (Greatcoats, #1) by Sebastien de Castell" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/books/1389310293s/18947303.jpg" alt="Traitor's Blade (Greatcoats, #1) by Sebastien de Castell" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10790290.Theft_of_Swords__The_Riyria_Revelations___1_2_" title="Theft of Swords (The Riyria Revelations, #1-2) by Michael J. Sullivan" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/books/1307959785s/10790290.jpg" alt="Theft of Swords (The Riyria Revelations, #1-2) by Michael J. Sullivan" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13452375.Legion__Legion___1_" title="Legion (Legion, #1) by Brandon Sanderson" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/books/1338512017s/13452375.jpg" alt="Legion (Legion, #1) by Brandon Sanderson" class="gr-hostedUserImg">

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1867558487" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1867558487" />
    <a title="Samir" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/52081294-samir"><img alt="Samir" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588945560p2/52081294.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1867558487?book_show_action=true">Jun 08, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Samir" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Samir" href="/user/show/52081294-samir">Samir</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780356509020" href="/book/show/34880234-kings-of-the-wyld">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1867558487" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1233726899609718524"><i>
  <b>“Then again, that was the point of being in the band, wasn’t it? A tiger, however fearsome, could be hunted into a corner. It fought alone, so it died alone. But to hunt a wolf was to constantly look over your shoulder, wondering if others were behind you in the dark.”</b>
</i><br/><br/><br/>This is a year of many great debuts so far and I think it is safe to presume that this will be one of the best, if not the best. This is one the best debuts I have ever read and I can't remember having so much fun since the <i>Lie</i></span>
  <span id="freeText1233726899609718524" style="display:none"><i>
  <b>“Then again, that was the point of being in the band, wasn’t it? A tiger, however fearsome, could be hunted into a corner. It fought alone, so it died alone. But to hunt a wolf was to constantly look over your shoulder, wondering if others were behind you in the dark.”</b>
</i><br><br><br>This is a year of many great debuts so far and I think it is safe to presume that this will be one of the best, if not the best. This is one the best debuts I have ever read and I can't remember having so much fun since the <i>Lies of Locke Lamora</i> and the <i>Theft of Swords</i>. That being said, this goes straight to my all-time favorites shelf.<br><br>There was a time when Saga was the best band of mercenaries in the known world and their escapades remained legendary even today because glory never gets old. Speaking of present times, mercenaries have changed; there were no more touring across the lands of Grandual and the notorious Heartwyld and killing whatever you were hired to kill. Mercenaries (bands) today are doing gigs in the arenas and the only thing they are after is fame. Clay Cooper, once a proud member of Saga, is living an ordinary life, enjoying the comforts of home with his wife and daughter. But then, an ex-bandmate turns up at his door asking for help. His daughter is trapped in the city under siege on the other side of the world and time has come to get the band back together for one last tour. <br><br>This is a tale about a quest with impossible odds, a quest that will take you on a fun adventure and you’ll be excited as Bilbo was when he was on his way to Erebor<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1496955239ra/22971884.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>but it is also a tale of friendship and camaraderie between a fantastic group of characters and you’ll have a hard time picking your favorite one. If you like hit first, ask questions later, always eager to fight warrior, then your pick would be Ganelon. If you like kind-hearted, goofy characters, Moog is your man. Or your wizard, your preference. For a laid-back hedonist type, look no further than Matrick. No one can dislike an adventurous and charismatic character like Gabe. The last, and most certainly not the least, a silent but strong type, which is, of course, Clay. The heart and soul of this group, reluctant to be considered as a hero or a leader of any kind and most eager to help those in need.<br><br>You can see straight away that Eames is fan of video games not just because of the quest like storyline but because of the vast number of RPG elements like the various creatures in this world, scenery, legendary weapons, armor and skyships. I think that is more than enough to make every fan of JRPGs and MMORPGs happy.<br> <br>I was an avid gamer when I was younger so I had my fair share of RPGs and reading this was like a trip down memory lane. This book is the best RPG I have never played. In addition, it also has the best soundtrack, well, if you’re a fan of classic rock like I am. Don’t let this observation mislead you; you don’t have to be a gamer to appreciate this book, this one will appeal to all fantasy fans alike and there are no sufficient words to recommend this fantastic book enough.<br><br>I mentioned the soundtrack so you’re probably wondering what the hell I’m on about. (Owl)Bear with me. If you go to the author’s web page you can find a lot of great stuff there like the map of the world, various art of the characters and yes, you guessed it, the soundtrack, which inspired Eames while he was writing. I was listening to these songs while reading and it worked great so not only did the author successfully managed to channel the spirit of the songs into the story but he also gave me a movie like experience as well. <br><br>Since I digressed into the topic of music, there’s nothing I can do now, I guess I’ll keep on rambling. Throughout this novel you’ll come across a lot of rock music easter eggs. For instance, the band’s name is Saga and I might be taking a shot in the dark here but I think that is an homage to the Canadian rock band of the same name, but there is one reference I’m very certain of and that is the Riot House, a place for mercenary bands to gather round and participate in all kinds of debauchery. Riot House was the nickname of the Hyatt Hotel in LA and it was a hotel of choice for touring rock bands in the 60s and the 70s like Led Zeppelin, the Rolling Stones, the Doors, the Who and the rest of the superstars of the era, and you can imagine what kind of stuff must have happened there and reading about it here made me grin with approval.<br><br>Even though this is a lighthearted and fun fantasy there were a lot of touching moments and as I was reading them I could almost swear someone was cutting onions nearby. Author did a great job of delivering scenes that put you through a roller coaster of emotions and it will make you appreciate this story even more.<br><br>One thing that I particularly enjoyed were the fighting sequences, they were gripping, energetic, suspenseful and mixed up with just the right dose of humor and every time they were done, I was craving for more. <br><br>I had so much fun reading this rollicking adventure and I would recommend it to all fantasy fans but especially to the fans of Michael J. Sullivan because of the way the characters are written and Scott Lynch because this novel has that kind of flair with its witty, sharp dialogues and plenty of twists and turns. <br><br><i>Kings of the Wyld</i> is the first book in <i>The Band</i> trilogy but it can be read as a standalone because the story wrapped up with no loose ends and next book in the series, <i>Bloody Rose</i>, will cast a new set of characters which I can’t wait to meet and accompany them on their adventure.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1233726899609718524" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2182231629" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2182231629" />
    <a title="Bradley" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4213258-bradley"><img alt="Bradley" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1508811508p2/4213258.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2182231629?book_show_action=true">Jan 27, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bradley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bradley" href="/user/show/4213258-bradley">Bradley</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=2018-shelf">2018-shelf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=humor">humor</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2182231629" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7418875966050049823">A battle of the bands! A total rock out with their cocks out. Well, swords, anyway.<br/><br/>I wasn't at all sure what I was going to make of this. I mean, epic fantasy is all great, but I was worried that it was just going to be another cookie-cutter, however well-written.<br/><br/>Not so! <br/><br/>In fact, it reads like a novel of aging rockers getting their lives out of the gutter to go on one last tour, not only recapturing the time that they were once the best of the best, but going out in a real blaze... just as long </span>
  <span id="freeText7418875966050049823" style="display:none">A battle of the bands! A total rock out with their cocks out. Well, swords, anyway.<br /><br />I wasn't at all sure what I was going to make of this. I mean, epic fantasy is all great, but I was worried that it was just going to be another cookie-cutter, however well-written.<br /><br />Not so! <br /><br />In fact, it reads like a novel of aging rockers getting their lives out of the gutter to go on one last tour, not only recapturing the time that they were once the best of the best, but going out in a real blaze... just as long as they hash out all their failings and pick up the pieces one last time as well. :)<br /><br />The novel is super fun on both sides of this mashup. It's a glory filled echo of all our most favorite old school rocker bands, their ignominy, their weaknesses, their absolute perfection. It's not only a road trip, but it's also one of the tightest character-driven novels I've seen in a long time. <br /><br />The other side is pure mercenary fantasy gold. I think just about every fantasy trope is treated as an old hat here, our world-weary tattooed rockers having already seen it all, done it all. Being fat and old and having lost a few magical weapons along the way is just the start of the tale, however, and getting their heart back is just as fun as the side quests.<br /><br />But damn. What A Ride. The whole novel is funny and tight and a pure delight from start to finish. Don't let the light tone fool you, either. All these characters feel real. And the blowout at the end? Holy crap! I haven't had quite this much fun with a new fantasy since... well, it feels like forever! (Not true, but I do go through a barbarian hoard of books.) :)<br /><br />I totally recommend this for... everyone who loves old school rock and anyone who loves bloody fantasy. :)<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7418875966050049823" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Scott  Hitchcock" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Scott  Hitchcock" href="/user/show/50894754-scott-hitchcock">Scott  Hitchcock</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/31698361-kings-of-the-wyld">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50894754-scott-hitchcock?shelf=2017-published-and-read">2017-published-and-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50894754-scott-hitchcock?shelf=grimdark">grimdark</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1947453994" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15733432002468678999">This book would be the fantasy partner of the sci-fi book <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9969571.Ready_Player_One' title='Ready Player One by Ernest Cline' rel='nofollow noopener'>Ready Player One</a> in that there's a myriad of references to pop culture, D&D, gaming, music of which a lot derives from the 80's. I got a lot of them. The ones I knew but couldn't quite place drove me mad. <br/><br/>The book reads like a D&D quest and our characters either had the cheat codes or an endless supply of quarters to make it through to the "battle of the bands" and get their names on the high scores list. That said the writing was excelle</span>
  <span id="freeText15733432002468678999" style="display:none">This book would be the fantasy partner of the sci-fi book <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9969571.Ready_Player_One" title="Ready Player One by Ernest Cline" rel="nofollow noopener">Ready Player One</a> in that there's a myriad of references to pop culture, D&amp;D, gaming, music of which a lot derives from the 80's. I got a lot of them. The ones I knew but couldn't quite place drove me mad. <br /><br />The book reads like a D&amp;D quest and our characters either had the cheat codes or an endless supply of quarters to make it through to the "battle of the bands" and get their names on the high scores list. That said the writing was excellent as was the humor interwoven to give us a break from the gore. I was cracking up a half hour later at times. I don't think the humor is for everyone but if you like sarcasm and innuendo you will. <br /><br />Looking forward to the next book in the series. </span>

<div id="review_2021904089" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2021904089" />
    <a title="Orient" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/43587353-orient"><img alt="Orient" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1500791761p2/43587353.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2021904089?book_show_action=true">Jun 17, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Orient" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Orient" href="/user/show/43587353-orient">Orient</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43587353-orient?shelf=2017">2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43587353-orient?shelf=desperado">desperado</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43587353-orient?shelf=br">br</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43587353-orient?shelf=entertaining">entertaining</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43587353-orient?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43587353-orient?shelf=hero">hero</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43587353-orient?shelf=killer">killer</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43587353-orient?shelf=bloody-romance">bloody-romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2021904089" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7712512787594085280"> <b>
  <i>We are each what the past has made of us.</i>
</b><br/><br/>What a peculiar book. When I started reading “Kings of Wyld” I was a bit distracted, couldn’t connect to the characters and felt like reading a random book, hah even thought of putting it on hold and read some other time. Putting my crappy POV aside, I was surprised as this book is really well written and it feels so. Though the story is not so unexpected or new (It reminded me of Joe Abercrombie), it’s quite quick-paced, it has monsters, peculiar hi</span>
  <span id="freeText7712512787594085280" style="display:none"> <b>
  <i>We are each what the past has made of us.</i>
</b><br><br>What a peculiar book. When I started reading “Kings of Wyld” I was a bit distracted, couldn’t connect to the characters and felt like reading a random book, hah even thought of putting it on hold and read some other time. Putting my crappy POV aside, I was surprised as this book is really well written and it feels so. Though the story is not so unexpected or new (It reminded me of Joe Abercrombie), it’s quite quick-paced, it has monsters, peculiar history, quite nice worldbuilding and of course characters, with interesting backstories and what’s more important, they aren’t fluffy. A bunch of comrades get back together to reunite the band for a noble cause. The most part of the story follows them in their perilous journey to reach that cause. Rather than presenting dashing young heroes as main characters, the author chose some older men with great experience and gripping old days to remember and repeat :) And they did it great!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380429186ra/859500.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>So what didn’t work for me at the start? IDK, if you do, please tell me and I’ll be most grateful :D <br><br>The moment I started liking this book is when I stumbled into arena with the guys and of course I loved all the monsters in action. Hah, had to wait for that a bit :)<br><br>The story told in “Kings of Wyld” has tasty cynical spices (I love it in my fantasy), it’s grim a bit (not so dark as Malazan) and of course it’s funny. Though, I must confess, the jokes didn’t always work for me. But for the biggest part it did.<br><br> <b>
  <i>“You look like shit, by the way. What happened to your face?”<br>Clay shrugged. “I was born this way.”<br>“Your momma keeps an axe in her womb, eh? Was thinking of trying that myself, to keep the boys out.”</i>
</b><br><br>What else I liked about this book is that not everything is explained in details, so some stuff must be gathered by the reader himself/herself. Oh and the fighting, well done scenes, with all the juicy bits and crunchy sounds :)<br><br>The baddie. Oh I liked this person a lot.<br><br>A tyrannical self-proclaimed ruler +check<br>Powerful with a large army as backup +check<br>A representative of almost lost race with peculiar life span and armory +check<br>A creepy pet +check<br>A backstory as an ex-adversary +check<br>A creepy appearance +check<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1492255587ra/22498390.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Sorry, I drooled there a bit, my apologies. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1497719769ra/23052666.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Well, he had one disadvantage, there wasn’t a lot moments with him, but I was also charmed by a certain angel :) Oh boy, she’s awesome!!!! &lt;3 The unexpectedness, toughness, kick-assesness, cool backstory and charming qualities!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1497719660ra/23052658.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Did I mention monsters? Oh yes, there are a lot them! *fangirling mode on* There’s wyverns, goblins, ogres, centaurs, dragons and a few I haven’t even heard of! Like kobolds or ettins.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1497719660ra/23052659.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The ending pretty summarizes the main themes of this book: courage, loyalty, friendship and family. That’s what matters. It definitely gave me a great satisfying feeling after finishing this book. <br><br>To sum up, “Kings of the Wyld” is a fun, entertaining read. It wasn’t mind-blowing for me but def a pleasant playdate, which I’ll be happy to continue with other books in this series. <br><br> <b>
  <i>And so it goes, thought Clay. Life was funny, and fickle, and often cruel. Sometimes the unworthy went on living, while those who deserved better were lost.<br>Or not lost, he considered, since they lingered on in the hearts of those who loved them, who love them still, their memory nurtured like a sprig of green in an otherwise desolate soul. Which was, he supposed, a kind of immortality, after all.</i>
</b><br><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="7712512787594085280" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1890910024" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17371114489562858660">Kings of the Wyld is an engaging and fun adventure where a band of mercenaries whose days have passed are coming together for a final time to rescue the daughter of their frontman.<br/><br/>This is an impressive debut which walks a fine line between epic and grimdark fantasy interspersed with humorous elements.<br/>It's a great tale of friendhip between mature characters who are in for something they might be way too old for. <br/>Although there is constant humor and a bunch of more or less well disguised pop-cultu</span>
  <span id="freeText17371114489562858660" style="display:none">Kings of the Wyld is an engaging and fun adventure where a band of mercenaries whose days have passed are coming together for a final time to rescue the daughter of their frontman.<br /><br />This is an impressive debut which walks a fine line between epic and grimdark fantasy interspersed with humorous elements.<br />It's a great tale of friendhip between mature characters who are in for something they might be way too old for. <br />Although there is constant humor and a bunch of more or less well disguised pop-culture references, the actual plot and characters are never put aside for it.<br /><br />This is well crafted fun that finds meaningful moments despite the characters slaughtering their way through an entire D&amp;D monster codex.<br />An uplifting read that found me in a mood where I needed it and at an age where I needed it. 5 stars, recommneded! <br /><br />My video review: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://youtu.be/80n4Ohl4Z8I">https://youtu.be/80n4Ohl4Z8I</a></span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2773369248?book_show_action=true">Apr 06, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emma" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emma" href="/user/show/28602001-emma">Emma</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2773369248" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15039097044762614074">Let me ask you a question, dear friends… Are you, perhaps, past your prime? Maybe a little out of shape? Or a lot?? Do you think your glory days are a thing of the past? Worry not, for this book is a shot of pure energy to the brain. So much damn potency it might succeed in dragging your aged body along for the ride. It’s a call to arms, a blaring hurrah, a vindication of the idea that you might still matter. Welcome, friends, to the Band.<br/><br/>Ok, ok, so I’m a little bit late to this. In fact, I’m so</span>
  <span id="freeText15039097044762614074" style="display:none">Let me ask you a question, dear friends… Are you, perhaps, past your prime? Maybe a little out of shape? Or a lot?? Do you think your glory days are a thing of the past? Worry not, for this book is a shot of pure energy to the brain. So much damn potency it might succeed in dragging your aged body along for the ride. It’s a call to arms, a blaring hurrah, a vindication of the idea that you might still matter. Welcome, friends, to the Band.<br /><br />Ok, ok, so I’m a little bit late to this. In fact, I’m so late all the best reviews have been written and I don’t have much to add. Save this: the book is fun. Pure entertainment. So much so that I even forgave the repeated <i>deus ex machina</i> moments... bloody airships turning up left, right, and centre. Anyway...<br /><br />I was in a reading slump before and now I’m not. Therefore the book is magic. <br /><br />For a more extensive discussion of why this book is <b>the shit</b>, please see Petrik’s amazing review: <br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://bit.ly/2OZyaTw">https://bit.ly/2OZyaTw</a></span>
