<div id="review_1971438806" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1971438806" />
    <a title="Liam Degnan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8180038-liam-degnan"><img alt="Liam Degnan" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1971438806?book_show_action=true">Aug 25, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Liam Degnan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Liam Degnan" href="/user/show/8180038-liam-degnan">Liam Degnan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8180038-liam-degnan?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1971438806" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3421071258325883651"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>"But life, Clay knew, didn't work that way. It wasn't a circle; you didn't go round and round again. It was an arc, its course as inexorable as the sun's trek across the sky, destined at its highest, brightest moment to begin its fall"</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/><b>
  <u> 3.5 Stars: ✰✰✰ ½.</u>
</b> <b>Full review is now up! Let me know what you think =].</b><br/><br/><b>Two things before I even write this review</b>: I really try to not be a "contrarian". Meaning that I try to never be that guy who bashes a good book just because everybody else lik</span>
  <span id="freeText3421071258325883651" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>"But life, Clay knew, didn't work that way. It wasn't a circle; you didn't go round and round again. It was an arc, its course as inexorable as the sun's trek across the sky, destined at its highest, brightest moment to begin its fall"</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br /><b>
  <u> 3.5 Stars: ✰✰✰ ½.</u>
</b> <b>Full review is now up! Let me know what you think =].</b><br /><br /><b>Two things before I even write this review</b>: I really try to not be a "contrarian". Meaning that I try to never be that guy who bashes a good book just because everybody else liked it and so they feel some kind of need to be different and complain about it. I hate it when people do that, because you can tell when people are just pulling at straws to find something wrong with a book, and I find it to be extremely distasteful. I'm saying this because <b>
  <i>a lot</i>
</b> of people loved this book, and while I definitely did enjoy it, I didn't love it like everybody else seemed to. And that's okay sometimes. This was definitely a good book, I just wasn't really feeling the level of hype that everybody else seemed to have.I try to always to be honest in my reviews, without being obnoxious towards people who liked the book, and without being disrespectful to the author. <br /><br />And that's the second thing worth mentioning - the author. Nicolas Eames seems like an awesome guy. He interacted with a bunch of us over at <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/192999-fantasy-buddy-reads?ref=nav_bar_discussions_pane_group" rel="nofollow noopener">Fantasy Buddy Reads</a>, which was awesome; and I've seen some of his conversations with people on their reviews. Genuinely seems like a great person, and he is clearly a gifted writer. He made me want to love this book, and while it wasn't my favorite book ever, I'm going to keep reading his books because I think that he has major potential in the fantasy genre. For a debut, this book was excellent. With that out of the way, I'll move on with my review.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>"Yet the deepest scars are often hidden, and though a mirror might reveal our weakness, it reflects only a fraction of our strength"</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br /><br /><b>
  <u>Prose:</u>
</b><br /><br />I need to talk a minute just to talk about the writing in this book, because <b>it was so unexpectedly good</b>. What everybody told me about this book did not expect me for the kind of writing that fills this book. Everybody quotes the jokes, the funny scenes, the banter ect. that fills this book, but beyond all of that, Eames is just a really good writer. Even if you look at just a few of the quotes I've included in my review, he is so good at getting you into the emotions of the character he's writing about. <br /><br />He has an almost poetic way of writing at times that seems COMPLETELY unsuited to the kind of book I was expecting to read. It was a very pleasant surprise, and in spite of the lighthearted quality of the story itself, I very much appreciated it. I wanted to highlight this first, because it was really the thing that drew me into the story.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>"Which are you, the monster or the man?.... The truth, he knew, was that the world needed his kind of monster"</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br /><br /><b>
  <u>Story &amp; Plot</u>
</b><br /><br />There was a lot of elements that felt good and bad to me concerning the story itself. I picked up this book because I <b>LOVED</b> the idea of a group of middle aged, has-been mercenaries coming back together (the whole "getting the band back together" for one final tour thing). It's an unoriginal idea used in a context that IS totally original, and the combination seemed really cool and appealing. That was awesome, and combined with really good writing, it seemed like we were going to get something really special. Great overall concept.<br /><br />Just considering the fact that the writing was so good, it actually left me kind of frustrated, because it felt wasted on what is ultimately an "okay" plotline. Other than the few elements that make it unique, the story itself felt like one I've heard before. A common problem within fantasy is that so many stories get boiled down to ANOTHER impossible rescue mission/damsel in distress/save the princess against-all-odds kind of tale. And this story was basically that, taken to an extreme extent. By the end of the book, <b>it seemed like WAY too much of the resolution boiled down to "magic"</b>, which was not satisfying to read about at all. Magic is not bad, but if you're going to solve your problems in a book using magic, it has to be foreshadowed and built up to. Otherwise, it feels like a lot of things were just pulled out of thin air, and there was far too much of this going on for my tastes. <br /><br />Overall, it wasn't in any way bad, just didn't grip me, and I felt like "magic" was overused by and large, which was a little disappointing. <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>"And now comes the quiet one, the gentle giant, he who fights his battles with a shield. Stout as a the tree that counts its age in aeons, constant as the star that marks true north and shines most brightly on the darkest nights."</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br /><br /><b>
  <u>Worldbuilding &amp; Characters:</u>
</b><br /><br /><b>The worldbuilding was another just "okay" thing to me</b>. Almost all of it was borrowed, from a myriad of different sources, and all of the references to other books, video games, RPGs, actual real-life bands, (ect.) became somewhat redundant to me. Different from Ready Player One, with outside references GALORE, it just didn't seem to really fit well with this book. It felt cheapish, and tended towards taking me *out* of the book, rather than drawing me deeper into it. <br /><br /><b>The characters in this book were great though</b>. Clay himself (the main perspective of this tale) was superbly developed, and Eames gives us plenty of glimpses into his past, his character, and his thoughts and experiences throughout the book. His companions are just as likeable, and all incredibly different from one another, which definitely added a lot to this book. Even the side characters we meet along the way, as well as the villains, were excellently portrayed. Eames gives us a lot of humor in the interactions between characters, <b>but there's also a heavy dose of reality in this book</b>, and the deep friendship portrayed between many of these characters was a cool thing to see in the midst of all the laughs. <br /><br />My one complaint regarding character development is that <b>I think my own enjoyment suffered due to the limited POV</b>. We only ever see things from Clay's perspective and don't get to know any of the other characters in the way we know him. I think the story could have benefitted from having more than one perspective, even if it wasn't among those in the band itself. The story centers around the band trying to save Gabriel's daughter Rose, but Rose has almost zero presence in the book. It would have been cool I think to occasionally have a POV from her perspective inside of Castia. My two cents =]. <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>"But even a coward found his courage in a corner, and there were things even a craven heart could not allow."</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br /><br /><b>
  <u>In Conclusion</u>
</b><br /><br />This was definitely a good book, and one that I will recommend to people in the future. A lot of people liked this book a heck of a lot more than I did, but even still, 3.5 is still pretty good by my standards. Based on what I know about Nicolas Eames, I think we only have good things to come from him, and I'm really looking forward to see what else he has to bring to the table. <br /><br />Happy reading =].<br /><br /><br />*******************************************<br /><br />Finally picking this back up, after my first failed attempt to read this a few months ago. Too many people loved it for me not to continue, so I'm starting from the very beginning, reading it in print this time =]. Hoping to love it as much as everybody else did!</span>
  <a data-text-id="3421071258325883651" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2021629185" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2021629185" />
    <a title="Sarah (thegirltheycalljones)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/32607699-sarah-thegirltheycalljones"><img alt="Sarah (thegirltheycalljones)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1569607878p2/32607699.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2021629185?book_show_action=true">Jun 30, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sarah (thegirltheycalljones)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sarah (thegirltheycalljones)" href="/user/show/32607699-sarah-thegirltheycalljones">Sarah (thegirltheycalljones)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Sarah (thegirltheycalljones) by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/59458347-petrik">Petrik</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32607699-sarah-thegirltheycalljones?shelf=petrik-s-holy-crusade">petrik-s-holy-crusade</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32607699-sarah-thegirltheycalljones?shelf=gorgeous-cover">gorgeous-cover</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32607699-sarah-thegirltheycalljones?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32607699-sarah-thegirltheycalljones?shelf=favourite-characters">favourite-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32607699-sarah-thegirltheycalljones?shelf=crew-team">crew-team</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32607699-sarah-thegirltheycalljones?shelf=great-male-lead">great-male-lead</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32607699-sarah-thegirltheycalljones?shelf=has-that-special-something">has-that-special-something</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32607699-sarah-thegirltheycalljones?shelf=book-boyfriend">book-boyfriend</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2021629185" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11694636759160027503"><b>Shamelessly editing this review on the sole purpose to remind you of the existence of this book. Christmas is coming, you know what to do! You're welcome.</b><br/><br/><i>I always say that I hardly ever give 5 stars to a book straight after finishing it, because I like to be sure, and 5 stars cannot be given lightly (yes, I'm such a pain in the ass sometimes). Well, screw it, screw my former 4 stars, this one gets a 5.<br/><br/>Also, I swear way too much below.</i><br/><br/><br/>Well, how fucking enjoyable was that! <br/>For the simple reason th</span>
  <span id="freeText11694636759160027503" style="display:none"><b>Shamelessly editing this review on the sole purpose to remind you of the existence of this book. Christmas is coming, you know what to do! You're welcome.</b><br /><br /><i>I always say that I hardly ever give 5 stars to a book straight after finishing it, because I like to be sure, and 5 stars cannot be given lightly (yes, I'm such a pain in the ass sometimes). Well, screw it, screw my former 4 stars, this one gets a 5.<br /><br />Also, I swear way too much below.</i><br /><br /><br />Well, how fucking enjoyable was that! <br />For the simple reason that there are too many fantasy books worth a shot for a lifetime, I don't think I would have ever found this one if not for the <s>caps locked supplication</s> wise rec from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1978164883?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Petrik</a> and man, I OWE YOU ONE! It took some balls to lure me in with the "If you like Scott Lynch" trick, but you were right and I regret nothing! :D <br /><br />Hollywood gave some tries at the "let's get the band back together" thing, more or less successfully (I fell asleep trying to watch Red twice, and couldn't bother to go through the 12 first minutes a third time) but even if it sounds like a classic, I don't think I ever came across a book about that.<br />Because sure, there's a quest, a big noble mission, adventures, monsters, allies, enemies, danger all around but most of all, there's friendship. <b>This is a tale about friendship, a tale about genuine benevolence, a tale about family in its widest definition. THE FEELS, guys! This book was so fucking intense!</b><br /><br />Can we first talk about the names? Because names are important, especially when you have no visual, except from the one you're creating in your head from scratch.<br />A name wisely chosen can make your character from good to mighty, and a lousy name can have the opposite effect. Well at least that's my opinion. Names matter to me (you're talking to a girl who names all her devices with care and who needed two days before being able to use her first IPhone in order to "be sure the name fits") (shut up), even more when it's about our heroes, the ones you're supposed to get and like (that's how most of our pets are named, after all) or hate but in any case <i>feel</i> - I mean, even I, who's not particularly fond of SJM to say the least, can admit that "Chaol Westfall" is a kick-ass name. Even in this painful Shoulda-Been-But-Wasn't disappointment best known as Pacific Rim (don't even get me started on Pacific Rim) you could find one of the coolest fictional names of the 21st Century : Stacker Pentecost (though in this case, it's Idris fucking ELBA : he'd still be the coolest dude in the room if he was called Glittering MacMoon-Moon).<br />Anyway, Clay Cooper, Gabriel "Golden Gabe", Matrick, Ganelon and Moog were spot on names if you ask me. <br />They show the past glory from their youth, they <i>sound</i> like band members names, they give them a personality and they got a certain panache. You <i>want</i> to feel connected to them just because you want to say their names out loud. Well, I did. And if that's not a good start, I don't know what is.<br />Also, I promise you there will be less brackets from now on. God this paragraph might have been a nightmare to read...<br /><br />I really liked how the author took all the lexical field of music and applied it to mercenaries. There were many winks to music on top of that (amongst others, if Valery is not a wink to Yoko Ono, please punch me in the face), and many pop culture references - but sometimes I wondered if it was only in my head (though nobody can mistake the "run, you fools" for something else).<br />Okay I did it again with the bloody brackets. I'll stop now.<br /><br />Some minor things bothered me a bit, so let's get them out of the way now, as I don't want to end this review on a somewhat negative note. Even if they seem so futile compared to my general enjoyment, I still need to point them out but they only affect the first half of the book:<br />&gt;&gt; the repetitions like, where this artifact came from. Once was enough, as it was explained pretty clearly in the first place. No need to remind us three times.<br />&gt;&gt; the narrator's urge to explain the dialogues : we're not morons, we can understand sarcasm or some unsaid things. It was breaking the momentum to be explained by voice-over some stuff they just said. (example : when the narrative/Clay points out "these aren't probabilities, they're threats" after Lastleaf speech at the meeting. No shit...)<br />Will I dare to say that with a tiny bit more editing, it would be easily better? It was certainly the reason why I needed time to be really into it. Not "into it" but to <i>care</i>, completely care about the characters. <br />For some chapters, I liked it but was wondering where it was willing to go. I was completely sucked in around 50%. Let me be clear : I was never bored before that, but I wasn't in love with the characters yet.<br /><br />Because yes, I'll say it again: at some moments I was a little in love with all of them (yes it's a wink to what you think it is). <br />Why?<br /><b> &gt;&gt; They're all complementary. </b> You cannot mistake one for the other, you cannot wonder if "this one could have been left out", they're all someone with a voice, a personality and a part to play.<br /><b> &gt;&gt; Mofo diversity! </b> In order to stay completely spoiler-free, I'll extend this point to every book character without naming any : you've got men, women, other...beings, you've got an openly gay dude with heterosexual male warrior friends, every skin colour you may dream of, a deadly woman respected by the deadliest warrior of the country, believers, non believers, and *drum rolls* a woman earning more money than her husband and <b>that doesn't bother him at all! And everybody else is fine with it too!</b> (yes, it is sad that I need to point that out...)<br /><b> &gt;&gt; These five guys, they're the ultimate definition of "friends". </b> They got each others back, no matter what. Pure friendship. They fucking love each others and that's fucking beautiful.<br />&gt;&gt; They made me laugh my ass off.<br />&gt;&gt; They made me cry.<br />&gt;&gt; Being in Clay's head is a wonderful thing.<br />&gt;&gt; I want <b>Moog</b> to be my Cool Uncle, I want to feed him cookies and to hug him forever.<br />&gt;&gt; I want to have drinks with <b>Matrick</b> and learn how to throw Roxy and Grace.<br />&gt;&gt; <b>I want Gabe to pep-talk me through life.</b> Like, he'd <i>literally</i> be next to me and cheer me up whenever needed. That SPEECH, guys... wow.<br />&gt;&gt; You don't want to know what I want to do with <b>Ganelon.</b><br />&gt;&gt; They're ALL hilarious in their own ways.<br />&gt;&gt; <b>I'll never get enough of Moog and Matrick's friendship</b> : every time they get reunited, they're basically 5 yeard old kids meeting up after summer break.<br />&gt;&gt; <b>They make you feel, because they're so damn human.</b> They're not the fearless hotshots they used to be. They were kings once, but now they're dads, they're old, they're scared. Their back hurts. But once, they were kings and deep down they still are. <br />They also know they didn't always do the right thing, that they were not always there when they needed to be. The way Clay reacts when Gabe comes to him for help is SO realistic. The way he feels when he realises where Ganelon has been all those years broke my heart. <br /><b>Clay Cooper might be a giant with a monster sleeping inside, but he's also a damn fine man. </b> (the fact he's totally Ron Perlman in my head is only a bonus)<br /><br />Two spoilery thoughts : <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Of course they'd need one healthy and fit warrior in their mad quest! Keeping Ganelon young was necessary; without him, their chances of survival would have been between none and...none. And the "how" was so very clever! <br /><br />CLAY FALLING FROM THE BRIDGE! I didn't see <i>that</i> coming! Oh how I loved being tricked, it's such a delight to be surprised - which unfortunately, doesn't happen to me that much with books or movies - and this one was perfect : how we knew something bad was about to happen when Kit stated that "the Cold Road takes its toll, always", and how we all thought it would be Dane&amp;Gregor? And how it was? But then CLAY? KABOOM!<br /> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />The secondary/side characters were cool too : special mention to Kit, Lady Jain, Larkspur and I just realised that I was about to list almost all the characters of the book, and that's pretty much pointless... <br /><br />Also, can we make a minute of silence for this : "Clay let out a breath he didn't know he'd been holding." xD<br /><br />The end broke me into a million of pieces (Petrik, sorry for the mental breakdown :D), I really liked it but was not prepared for a real end? I'm so used to series of many books that seeing real closure after a single one made me panic like hell... <br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Also, Kit's tale at the end was very cryptic and I need to reread it again with a clear mind. I'm pretty sure I missed some stuff, and I hope the things I didn't get will be explained in the next book... It's very hard to have to say goodbye to this band so soon! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><b>To sum it up :</b> You know how sometimes there's a minor theme in the background which is denied by everybody except one, and it's so not subtle that you <i>know</i> this specific thing will eventually come up? And how it can be so eyeroll-worthy when it does? Well here, by the time it happened I was only SO VERY happy! <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I'm talking about Moog and owlbears (that can also work for Moog and the rot) <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />That's honestly the best example I can give to say this book is a complete success despite its tiny flaws. It manages to turn some of its flaws into great moments, just because the characters are awesome.<br /><br /><b>Those guys made it on the favourite characters shelf in a heartbeat. I highlighted the hell out of my Kindle and I let you the immense joy to discover those quotes by yourself. Because right now, what you have to do is go buy this precious piece of wonder.<br />Thank you, Nicholas Eames. You're a star.</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="11694636759160027503" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('AFrV3oTLl+PTZeD2wGbvje0Ct295c6FT5pILroJFcgv+uJphjn5sn8v2wvbbD6wBJkbcV3XWz0XOAVnQYryNqg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('oqZoUAOaIUiplU47K0LjM0Pr5FV+Lh2mH09Fld+ezzZcRCfvCS/aNLEGbDswK6C/iK+PbXKLc7A33BfrP2cwlw==')})
  }

One in every hundred men is able to magically transform himself into a bigger, stronger, faster killing machine.\n\nEveryone else is fodder, destined to fight and die in the endless war. Young, gift-less Tau knows all this, but he has a plan of escape. He\'s going to get himself injured, get out early, and settle down to marriage, children, and land. Only, he doesn\'t get the chance. Those closest to him are brutally murdered, and his grief swiftly turns to anger. Fixated on revenge, Tau dedicates himself to an unthinkable path.       <div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/work/quotes/51246585-kings-of-the-wyld">Quotes from Kings of the Wyld</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;Among them is a renegade king, he who sired five royal heirs without ever unzipping his pants. A man to whom time has imparted great wisdom and an even greater waistline, whose thoughtless courage is rivalled only by his unquenchable thirst.<br /><br />At his shoulder walks a sorcerer, a cosmic conversationalist. Enemy of the incurable rot, absent chairman of combustive sciences at the university in Oddsford, and the only living soul above the age of eight to believe in owlbears.<br /><br />Look here at a warrior born, a scion of power and poverty whose purpose is manifold: to shatter shackles, to murder monarchs, and to demonstrate that even the forces of good must sometimes enlist the service of big, bad motherfuckers. His is an ancient soul destined to die young.<br /><br />And now comes the quiet one, the gentle giant, he who fights his battles with a shield. Stout as the tree that counts its age in aeons, constant as the star that marks true north and shines most brightly on the darkest nights.<br /><br />A step ahead of these four: our hero. He is the candle burnt down to the stump, the cutting blade grown dull with overuse. But see now the spark in his stride. Behold the glint of steel in his gaze. Who dares to stand between a man such as this and that which he holds dear? He will kill, if he must, to protect it. He will die, if that is what it takes.<br /><br />“Go get the boss,” says one guardsman to another. “This bunch looks like trouble.”<br /><br />And they do. They do look like trouble, at least until the wizard trips on the hem of his robe. He stumbles, cursing, and fouls the steps of the others as he falls face-first onto the mud-slick hillside.&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
              &mdash;
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/quotes/8286902-among-them-is-a-renegade-king-he-who-sired-five">79 likes</a>
            </nobr>
            <div class="clear"></div>
          </div>
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;But what does a mirror know? What can it show us of ourselves? Oh, it might reveal a few scars, and perhaps a glimpse—there, in the eyes—of our true nature. The spirit beneath the skin. Yet the deepest scars are often hidden, and though a mirror might reveal our weakness, it reflects only a fraction of our strength.&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
              &mdash;
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/quotes/8302275-but-what-does-a-mirror-know-what-can-it-show">55 likes</a>
            </nobr>
            <div class="clear"></div>
          </div>
